Zu Ti 133

— Ru Bi

Not long after the founding of the Jin Dynasty, because Emperor Hui was too foolish, the empire was thrown into great chaos. Initially, there were eight imperial princes—Prince Lun of Zhao, Prince Jiong of Qi, Prince Ying of Chengdu, Prince Yong of Hejian, Prince Yi of Changsha, Prince Yue of Donghai, Prince Zhang of Chu, and Prince Mo of Nanyang—who fought each other for power and profit, killing and driving each other away, causing endless turmoil. At this time, Liu Yuan, the Left Worthy Prince of the Xiongnu, saw the great chaos in the Jin Dynasty as a good opportunity to seize the empire. Therefore, he was unwilling to be a vassal state of the Jin Dynasty and ascended to the throne as emperor, establishing the Han Dynasty. Because Liu Yuan considered himself the nephew of the Han Dynasty, inheriting the throne as a nephew inheriting his uncle's position, he named his dynasty Han.

Soon after, Liu Yuan died, and his son Liu Cong inherited the throne. At this time, the internal affairs of the Jin Dynasty were even more chaotic. Liu Cong ordered his generals Shi Le, Liu Yao, and Huyan Yan to lead troops to attack the Jin Dynasty. How could the Jin troops resist? Emperors Huai and Min were captured by the Han troops one after another, and were subsequently killed by Liu Cong. As a result, the areas north of the Yangtze River were occupied by the Xiongnu generals.

Fortunately, the areas south of the Yangtze River remained peaceful. A member of the Jin imperial clan, General of Pacifying the East and military governor of Yangzhou and the southern regions of the Yangtze River, Langya King Rui, ascended the throne in Nanjing. By employing capable individuals such as Wang Dao, he managed to safeguard the southern regions.

At this time, the entire northern part of China was in the hands of foreigners. The Han Dynasty was established by the Xiongnu people, with its capital in Pingyang (later changing its dynastic title to Former Zhao). Shi Le, a Jie from Wudu and originally a general under Liu Yuan, later rebelled, destroyed the state established by the Di people, and established the Later Zhao Dynasty. In addition, there were the Former Yan Dynasty established by the Xianbei Murong clan, the Former Liang Dynasty established by the Di people Zhang Gui, the Dai state established by the Xianbei Tuoba clan, and the Former Qin Dynasty established by the Di people Fu Jian. The Former Qin was the most powerful, and it almost unified northern China and even wanted to destroy the Jin Dynasty, which was clinging to power in the south of the Yangtze River.

This era is known in Chinese history as the "Five Barbarians' Uprising in China."

Zu Ti was born in this era of great turmoil.

Zu Ti, styled Shiya, was from Fanyang. His father died when he was still a child. He had a very forthright temperament, was generous in giving, and practiced chivalry. Although he was already fourteen or fifteen years old and had not yet made progress in his studies, his brothers were very worried. However, whenever he went to the villages, he would distribute money, rice, cloth, and silk to the poor according to his own will, practicing the principle of "everyone eats when there is food, and everyone uses when there is money." Those who received his assistance thanked him, but he said, "Don't thank me, my brothers told me to distribute these to you. You should thank my brothers."

Zu Ti had several good brothers who not only did not blame him for giving away money, rice, cloth, and silk, but praised him. Because they all felt that money, rice, cloth, and silk were ultimately things that one could not bring into life or take away in death. Using them to help people was what a great man should do. Therefore, they worked hard to do good deeds. Soon, they were highly respected. Anyone who knew the Zu Ti brothers held them in high regard, saying that they would be men of great use in the future.

Year after year passed, and Zu Ti's age gradually increased, and his reputation grew with his age. One day, Zu Ti thought to himself, "Now I have a reputation, but where is my real knowledge? It's just an empty name. If I just continue to be generous, practice chivalry, and do good deeds for the rest of my life, what good will it do for the country and society? Today, the world is in chaos, and it is the time for heroes to repay the country. But without the talent to deal with this chaotic situation, there is nothing I can do. I want to be a useful person, to learn the skills to deal with this situation, and I must find these skills in books. I should study."

Therefore, Zu Ti resolved to study. He diligently read the classics, histories, philosophical works, and literary collections, as long as the books were useful. If he didn't have them at home, he would buy them or borrow them. After reading for several years, Zu Ti's mind was filled with reason.

Zu Ti had a very close friend named Liu Kun, who was also a very handsome young man. They studied literature and practiced martial arts together, and they both had the ambition to drive out the barbarians and restore China. With shared goals and common interests, they became very close.

Sometimes, Zu Ti and Liu Kun would forget the time while studying literature and practicing martial arts, and it would be late at night, so they would rest together. As dawn approached, the rooster raised by the family would stretch its neck and crow. Zu Ti woke up, heard the rooster crowing, and nudged Liu Kun, saying, "Brother, listen, the rooster is crowing. This crowing is very good for people. It's telling people: it's almost dawn, the light is coming soon, everyone get up! Brother, let's not let it down."

Liu Kun also turned over and got up, saying, "Exactly, let's not let it down." So Zu Ti and Liu Kun both drew their swords and danced in the room, the flashing sword light mixing with the lamplight.

After the two finished dancing with their swords, they sat facing each other under the lamp, resting for a while. Zu Ti said, "Now the eight princes are at odds, turning the empire into a mess. The barbarians are taking this opportunity to invade. It seems that the Jin Dynasty won't last long. We have good skills and have learned both literature and martial arts. We should take this opportunity to repay the country. Even if the Jin Dynasty is destroyed, we must do our best to revive China, that is the right thing to do!"

After listening, Liu Kun said, "That's right, we have the same aspirations, and we should do what we can. In the future, when we achieve merit and establish our careers, neither of us should yield to the other. Let's see who achieves his ambition first, that will be a good man. Brother, look, the Central Plains relies on mountains and rivers, a good battlefield. It is a good place for you and me to drive out the barbarians and gallop on horseback."

The two looked at each other and couldn't help but clap their hands and laugh.

Before Emperor Yuan of Jin ascended the throne, he had already heard of Zu Ti's reputation. Now that he had become emperor in Jiangfu and wanted to restore the dynasty, he naturally needed some capable people. Therefore, he issued an edict appointing Zu Ti as Military Counselor (similar to the position of a military advisor). At this time, Zu Ti already had two hundred trusted followers, all of whom were burly men, loyal, righteous, and possessing outstanding martial skills.

At that time, Emperor Yuan had just ascended the throne and was focused on pacifying the southern regions of the Yangtze River. He had no intention of crossing the river to the north to recover the lost territories.

One day during the early court session, Zu Ti stepped forward and reported, "The Jin Dynasty has come to this point not because the ruler is unprincipled, nor because the people are rebelling, but because the eight princes are at odds, fighting among themselves, and not defending the borders. That's why the barbarians have taken advantage of the situation and occupied the Central Plains. Now, the people of the Central Plains have suffered under the barbarians, and everyone wants the restoration of China. Everyone wants the government to send troops. They can all rise up to kill the barbarians. If Your Majesty can send generals and troops, I am willing to be the vanguard and cross the river to the north. At that time, the heroes of the Central Plains will surely respond like the wind, and the heroes of the southern regions of the Yangtze River will surely abandon their families and join the army. The lost territories can be recovered, and the national shame can be washed away. What is Your Majesty's will?"

Emperor Yuan was very moved by Zu Ti's words and immediately appointed Zu Ti as General of Mighty Valor and Governor of Yuzhou. However, there were no troops to send, so he had to give him three thousand bolts of cloth and enough grain for one thousand people, and ordered Zu Ti to recruit troops and act accordingly.

After receiving the decree, Zu Ti returned home, made some preparations, and ordered ships to be prepared to cross the river to the north. Since the court had no troops to send, Zu Ti only took his two hundred personal followers across the river.

As the ship was in the middle of the river, Zu Ti suddenly stood up, raised his hand, struck the oar, and solemnly said, "Zu Ti is determined to cross the river to the north. If I do not recover the Central Plains and kill all the barbarians, I will not cross this river even in death! If I cross, I will surely die in this river!"

Zu Ti's face was very serious when he spoke, and his voice was passionate and intense. The two hundred followers were all moved by his words. Everyone clenched their fists and rubbed their palms, eager to fight the barbarians, recover the lost territories, and wash away the national shame!

After crossing the Yangtze River, Zu Ti established his main camp in Huaiyin. On one hand, he rushed to manufacture armor and weapons, and on the other hand, he raised a large banner with the words "Loyalty and Righteousness" and recruited heroes. Soon, patriots from the Yellow River and Yangtze River regions had joined Zu Ti's command, numbering two thousand people.

After training these two thousand people, Zu Ti advanced his troops, first resolving those miscellaneous troops who were ostensibly militia but were actually traitors by either disbanding them or accepting their surrender. Only then did he formally engage in battle with the troops of Shi Le of Later Zhao. Shi Hu, Shi Le's nephew, was a famous general known throughout the land, but he was defeated by Zu Ti through trickery, and all the barbarian generals lost their courage. As a result, the people in the Yellow River region who had not forgotten their homeland responded to Zu Ti. Shi Le's soldiers and generals could not hold their ground and fled. The areas south of the Yellow River were all recovered. Shi Le, fearing Zu Ti's power, sent people to Zu Ti's hometown to protect his ancestral tombs and sent people to Zu Ti to negotiate peace and trade. Zu Ti outwardly ignored Shi Le, but secretly allowed the people to trade. As a result, Zu Ti had well-trained soldiers and sufficient supplies. When he had the opportunity, he would cross the Yellow River to recover the lost territories of northern China.

Unexpectedly, at this time, Emperor Yuan sent Dai Yuan as Inspector-General to divide Zu Ti's military power. In the court, Wang Dun and Liu Wei were fighting for power, and an internal conflict was likely to break out. Zu Ti knew that once an internal conflict broke out, he would not be able to cross the Yellow River again to recover the lost territories, so he became depressed and fell seriously ill. As he was dying, Zu Ti lamented, "I have not completely recovered the lost territories before dying. I will not rest in peace even in death!"

He died in Chengdu in August of the twenty-fifth year.

Archimedes (287-212 B.C.) 134

— Yao Hua

Archimedes was a famous Greek physicist and geometer. He was born in Syracuse, a city on the island of Sicily. When he was born, the glorious era of Syracuse had already passed, and throughout his life, there were constant wars. Initially, King Pyrrhus of Epirus helped Syracuse fight the Carthaginians. Later, Pyrrhus, due to the jealousy and conspiracies of his allies, angrily led his troops back to his country. At that time, Archimedes was only eleven years old, and he had already entered school in Alexandria.

We are not very familiar with Archimedes' life in his youth, but we know that he had a serious and calm mind and spent many years in academic research, which enabled him to achieve his later accomplishments.

He had relations with the Syracuse royal family. He once said a famous bold statement to King Hiero, saying that if he were given a place to stand, he could move the Earth. But Hiero did not believe him. It just so happened that King Hiero was building a ship for King Ptolemy, but after its completion, no one in the entire city of Syracuse could figure out how to launch the ship. Archimedes then agreed to take on this task. He then came up with the organization of pulleys, which could use very little force to push a very large weight. After he arranged the pulleys, he handed one end of the rope to Hiero to pull. The ship, which could not be moved, was easily launched into the water by Hiero pulling the rope.

This success made the king trust him very much. Then came the second problem. King Hiero had commissioned a pure gold crown and wanted to know if the craftsman had mixed other metals into it, so he asked Archimedes to check it. The crown could not be broken, and visual observation was useless. Archimedes thought for a long time but could not solve the problem, so he had to reply to the king that there was no way. But he was always a competitive person, and he was very disappointed that this matter was unsuccessful. On his way back, he was very bored and listlessly ran to the public bathhouse to take a bath. When he jumped into the water, the water in the tub overflowed, and he noticed that the more he sank, the lighter his body seemed to feel. The clever Archimedes saw this phenomenon and was overjoyed. He jumped out of the tub and ran into the street, shouting, "I've got it! I've got it!" Because he had realized the famous law of buoyancy.

Archimedes, because he had a clear mind and was willing to think carefully, quickly deduced a conclusion from this phenomenon. Ordinary people, although they also saw the water overflowing from the tub when bathing and felt that their body seemed lighter, did not find the reason because they were too lazy to think and investigate.

Archimedes' law of buoyancy states that the buoyant force experienced by an object in water must be equal to the weight of the water displaced by the same volume. From this, the density or specific gravity of an object can be determined. Archimedes found that the specific gravity of the crown was lighter than the specific gravity of pure gold, so he concluded that the craftsman had mixed other metals into it.

A few years later, Archimedes grew old, and King Hiero died. He was succeeded by Hieronymus, the young king, who allied with Carthage, the sworn enemy, against Rome. As a result, the Roman navy blockaded the port of Syracuse, and General Marcellus led a large army to besiege the city of Syracuse.

Although Archimedes did not agree with the alliance with Carthage, when the country was in danger, he abandoned his personal views and used his intelligence and talent to come up with various defensive tools to protect his compatriots.

As mentioned above, Archimedes invented the organization of pulleys, which could use very little force to move a very large weight. Later, he invented the crane. Although this crane cannot be compared with modern cranes, more than two thousand years ago, Archimedes used it to lift Roman warships, suspend them in the air, and then drop them, colliding them with the water surface, smashing the Roman warships to pieces. Sometimes he lifted the ships into the city and lowered them to allow the people of Syracuse to capture these Roman soldiers alive.

He also invented the catapult, which could shoot large stones to attack Roman warships. He also invented a device that could shoot small stones and broken pieces of copper and iron to attack the enemy.

These inventions were powerful tools to help the people of Syracuse defend their country. The Roman army was terrified when they saw a rope thrown out of the city, fearing that the old scientist would come up with new ways to deal with them. Marcellus knew that morale was low and that the siege would not be effective, so he abandoned the attack on the city and adopted a blockade method, cutting off the food supply. In this way, Syracuse finally surrendered in 212 BC. Two years later, Rome ruled the entire island of Sicily.

When the city of Syracuse fell, the old scientist was buried in research, trying to save his compatriots through scientific inventions.

Although Marcellus suffered at the hands of Archimedes, he admired his talent very much. Therefore, on the day the city fell, he ordered his subordinates not to harm the old scientist. But he was not a person who was greedy for life and afraid of death. He had long been determined to die for his country. So when a soldier broke into his house, he unceremoniously shouted, "Get out, you fool, don't destroy my circles!" He deliberately angered the soldier and used the enemy's sword to end his own life.

Archimedes made significant contributions to geometry, hydrostatics, and mechanics throughout his life. In terms of his achievements, he is immortal even in death.

In geometry, he determined the ratio of the circumference of a circle to its diameter and the area of a circle. Although Epollonius also determined the value of pi (i.e., the ratio of the circumference to the diameter) at the same time, which was more accurate than Archimedes' determination, he stumped Epollonius with the famous "Cattle Problem." It is said that the answer to this problem was written in a book of more than six hundred pages.

In hydrostatics, he discovered the law of buoyancy and deduced other laws of hydrostatics from it, laying the foundation for hydrostatics. His two books on "Floating Bodies" are the bible for researchers of hydrostatics.

In mechanics, his contributions were also significant. He discovered the law of levers and manufactured pulleys and primitive cranes. These have a very close relationship with the daily lives of modern people! His basic theories of mechanics have not made any progress in more than two thousand years. It can be said that we are still in his world today.

Publishing World

Introduction to "The Essence of National High School and Junior High School Compositions" 135

— Zhou Hanmei

Writing is an important tool for recording events, expressing emotions, and conveying meanings. It is indispensable for both studying and managing affairs. Literature can cultivate the mind and exercise thinking, nurturing morality and serving as an important course in youth training, occupying a primary position in educational value. Observing history, the rise and fall, order and chaos of dynasties are often fully expressed in literature. We dare not say that literature can determine order and chaos, but at least it can express the spiritual trends of a certain era.

However, the scope of literature is very broad. Even with the Chinese language subject in middle schools, selecting materials for teaching is more difficult than other subjects. In terms of guiding extracurricular assignments, it is even more difficult to find an appropriate method. How to choose books of Chinese studies to cultivate a foundation in writing, how to emphasize composition methods and styles to train the ability of appreciation and discrimination of general scholars, how to cultivate the ability to express oneself, and how to guide scholars' writing, all these are major issues that Chinese language teachers have pondered for thousands of years, and have not yet been resolved. These points seem to focus too much on specialized issues in Chinese language teaching. Now, let's focus on the "observation" aspect. Observation is the most effective method in Chinese language teaching. Often, when a teacher presents a good work by a student to other students for viewing, the students' attention, research, and criticism are probably more serious than reading Chinese language teaching materials. If that article is published in a newspaper or magazine, the admiration and appreciation of the students will be even greater. And the student who wrote this article will be overjoyed and consider it a special honor. This situation, from childhood to old age, remains the same, regardless of ancient times, modern times, China, or foreign countries. However, the environment is changing, and the desire for pursuit is increasing. Therefore, in the Chinese language subject in elementary and middle schools, if teachers make full use of this observation method, the author believes that students' writing performance will definitely improve rapidly, and it can increase unlimited interest!

Here, we should pay attention to this "observation" method. If it is limited to one grade or one school, then the world is too small, and the scope is too narrow, and we cannot achieve our ideal effect. If we can collect the writing performance of students from middle schools across the country in one volume, then the students' observation materials will be rich, and the interest in observation will increase tenfold, and the benefits will be far greater than one grade or one school.

Mr. Ma Chonggan, in addition to politics and lecturing, suddenly made a grand vow to promote the advancement of middle school students throughout China. He invited famous scholars to carefully evaluate the writing performance of students from middle schools across the country. There were strict standards for subject matter, style, rhetoric, and composition, with careful selection and omission. He spent more than a year of hard work to compile this book, "The Essence of National High School and Junior High School Compositions." After browsing through it, the author deeply sighed at the hard work of the book's editor and the greatness of his contribution, and the deep benefits for middle school students across the country. And the Chinese language teachers of general middle schools will also find it very convenient.

The book is divided into two parts, one is "The Essence of National Junior High School Compositions," with four thick volumes; the other is "The Essence of National High School Compositions," with four thick volumes. These two parts of high school and junior high school composition essence include 1,274 articles, from 264 schools. It is impossible to collect all the writing performance of middle schools across the country, but it can already represent the writing performance of middle school students. Among them are narrative essays, explanatory essays, argumentative essays, book reviews, descriptive essays, biographical essays, applied essays, speeches, birthday essays, farewell essays, elegies, novels, poems, and plays, encompassing everything, and because of the careful selection, the abundance of masterpieces, there is no need to elaborate.

The author hereby introduces these two books to the Chinese language teachers and middle school students of middle schools across the country, hoping that each middle school student will have a copy and read it carefully. You should know that the ability to make good use of writing tools is the key to one's professional achievements in life; for the country, it is the key to the rise and fall of a generation's culture, and it is absolutely not to be ignored.

Friendly people in neighboring countries are saying: "Two hundred years later, the pronunciation and meaning of Chinese characters will need to be taught by them." We don't need to be angry that these words are too arrogant. In short, the fact that not every Chinese person is willing to study their own characters carefully and diligently is a painful fact that cannot be denied. "Why come? Just remember!"

"The Essence of Junior High School Compositions" has four thick volumes, each costing two yuan and two jiao, each volume costing five jiao and five fen; "The Essence of High School Compositions" has four thick volumes, and the selling price is the same as "The Essence of Junior High School Compositions." Published by Qinfen Bookstore on Simalu, Shanghai.

Extracurricular Activities 136

— Chen Jiyun

— Published by The Commercial Press, written by Li Xiangxu, et al.

Price per volume: National currency 3 yuan

Extracurricular activities are regarded by many modern educators as equally important as in-class work. Deam and Bear of the United States once said: "Extracurricular activities supplement and extend the experiences children gain in regular classes. They give proper outlets for children's surplus energy, natural tendencies of boys and girls, and self-respect; at the same time, they discover their ordinary and special abilities. The establishment of education is not to create energy, but to discharge and guide it. Extracurricular activities help develop the nature of young people, allowing these natural abilities to be fully expressed. Furthermore, extracurricular activities channel students' energy in beneficial directions, enabling them to receive good civic training." From this passage, we can understand the importance of extracurricular activities.

In the past, Chinese education generally regarded the purpose of education purely as the infusion of knowledge and the cultivation of morality. Therefore, the reading life of scholars was one of "ten years of cold window," without stepping into gardens or peeking through doors, spending all day reading books, even day and night, with no leisure. Those running schools only strictly supervised leisure education, not allowing the slightest bit of freedom. Chinese history clearly tells us that from the beginning of recorded history until the late Qing dynasty, the Chinese school administrative system never paid attention to extracurricular activities, let alone dreamed of them.

The history of extracurricular activities in our country is very short from beginning to end. Although the development is rapid, it is still immature. Although it has broken away from the budding stage, it is still a tender sapling in the garden; it relies on sound organization as its roots, precise administration as its soil, appropriate guidance and management as its rich and inexhaustible fertilizer, and all the visitors to the garden as its charitable protectors. We must constantly cut grass, constantly irrigate, let it grow, and when the time comes, it will naturally bear bright buds, beautiful flowers, and fragrant and unparalleled fruits.

How can "extracurricular activities" gradually develop? That, of course, requires educators to study. Regarding works on the study of extracurricular activities, there are only scattered articles in newspapers and magazines; systematic writings are still not many. Recently, The Commercial Press published "Extracurricular Activities" from the University Series, compiled by Mr. Li Xiangxu and others. Now, a brief introduction to the contents of the book is given below:

Chapter 1: Introduction

Details the definition of extracurricular activities, the types of extracurricular activities, the theoretical basis of extracurricular activities, the social purpose of extracurricular activities and education, and the goals of extracurricular activities and Chinese secondary education.

Chapter 2: A Brief History of Extracurricular Activities

The history of extracurricular activities is explained in two points: first, the history of Western extracurricular activities, divided into ancient and medieval periods, and modern and contemporary periods; second, the history of Chinese extracurricular activities, divided into before and after the eighth year of the Republic.

Chapter 3: Defects and Problems of Extracurricular Activities

Details the defects caused by external forces, its own defects, the opinions of various secondary school principals on defects and problems, the opinions of various secondary school students on defects and problems, and the prevention and remedy of defects.

Chapter 4: The Relationship between Extracurricular Activities and Various Subjects

Details that extracurricular activities not only do no harm but can also be helpful in the work of various subjects. It is explained from the principles of extracurricular activities and learning, extracurricular activities and design, and the impact of extracurricular activities on academic performance.

Chapters 5 and 6: Organization and Administration of Extracurricular Activities

The general principles of extracurricular activity organization and administration, the steps of extracurricular activity organization, examples of general American secondary school extracurricular activity organization and management, centralization and unification of administration, supply of time, and the need for forms are all explained in detail.

Chapter 7: Student Participation and Management

Details the principles of student participation management, student participation management methods, impropriety of depriving the right to participate in activities, encouragement of participation, point system, parallel system of service points and honor points, and prevention of the generation of useless organizations.

Chapter 8: Guidance of Extracurricular Activities

Divided into guidance system, principals and guidance, teachers and guidance, instructors, etc.

Chapters 9 and 10: Student Self-Government Association

Regarding the purpose of the student self-government association, the history of the student self-government association, the types of student self-government association, the scope of activities of the student self-government association, the organizational steps of the student self-government association, the administrative essentials of the student self-government association, the charter of the student self-government association, etc., are all explained in great detail.

Chapter 11: Group Meetings and Class Meetings

The value of group meetings, the functions of group meetings, the organization of group meetings, the activities of group meetings, the instructors of group meetings, the meeting time of group meetings; class meetings and student self-government associations, the activities of class meetings, the organization of class meetings, etc., are all explained in detail.

Chapter 12: Student Weekly Meetings

Details the importance of student weekly meetings, the goals of student weekly meetings, general criticisms, the scope of weekly meeting work, the undertaking of weekly meeting order, the date and time of weekly meetings, the allocation of weekly meeting order items, the organization of weekly meeting committees, weekly meetings hosted by class rotation, the value of weekly meetings, etc. (To be continued)

The Doubting Antiquity School and the Social History School (Continued) 137

— Yi Fu

In the conclusion, Gu stated that he praised the lively attitude of the social history school. I do not participate in the social history debate because of insufficient ability, but only take the review of materials as my own work. I offer this paper specifically to the social history school, but I hope that the propaganda documents of the pre-Qin philosophers should not be used as historical materials of ancient society, and attention should be paid to the danger of building pavilions on the sand. ...

Although Gu released an arrow at the social history school, it was well-intentioned and still relied on the social history school. Autumn Fishing Season Has Arrived Three Banks Raise Funds to Lend to Fishermen Totaling 120,000 Yuan Eight Loan Measures 140

The Four Banks Savings Society, Zhonghui Bank, and Xinhua Bank have raised 120,000 yuan to lend to fishermen first, as the autumn fishing season has arrived and fishermen are in urgent need of funds. The loan measures and progress are recorded as follows:

Three Banks Raise Funds

The preparation of the Fishery Syndicate has been nearly half a year. Although the Ministry of Industry has formulated an organizational outline and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for approval, all detailed measures have been drafted by Qian Xinzhi, Kui Yanfang, and Wang Zhixin, and have been submitted to the ministry for instructions. After receiving the letter, they can start drafting. However, the autumn fishing season is about to end. Fishing boats going to sea have always been advanced by fish companies. This year, due to the impact of the economic downturn, fishing boats have no way to borrow money and lack funds to go to sea. The Fish Market was requested and agreed to by the Four Banks Savings Society, Zhonghui, and Xinhua Banks to raise 120,000 yuan first. Xinhua Bank was entrusted to handle the loan, and 50,000 yuan has been lent to the Ningbo Fishermen's Cooperative to re-lend to the fishermen. The remaining 70,000 yuan will be lent to the fishing boats. Applications were made to the syndicate by the unloaders of the Fish Market and closed on the 20th. After review, loans can be started within days.

Loan Measures

There are eight articles recorded later: (1) The Four Banks Savings Society, Zhonghui Bank, and Xinhua Bank (hereinafter referred to as the Three Banks) are organizing ship industry loans for the 25th year of the autumn fishing season to meet the urgent needs of fishermen. (2) The purpose of the loan referred to in these measures is to lend to fishermen or ice-fresh boat merchants for a portion of the expenses required for this year's voyage. (3) The loan referred to in these measures is temporarily aimed at fishery cooperatives and unloaders in the Shanghai Fish Market and is temporarily limited to those related to the Shanghai Fish Market. (4) Those who apply for a loan in accordance with these measures must have the Shanghai Fish Market as a guarantor. When the Three Banks deem it necessary, they may also order the borrower to add individuals or groups recognized by the Three Banks as guarantors. The guarantor and the borrower jointly bear all the responsibilities for the repayment of the loan. (5) Those who apply for a loan in accordance with these measures take the payment that should be obtained from the sale of fish in the Shanghai Fish Market or the commission that should be obtained from the consignment as collateral. When the Three Banks recognize that the payment commission is insufficient as collateral, they may order the borrower to provide other collateral. (6) The loan period shall not exceed ten months, but it can be repaid in installments, and the interest decreases with the principal. (7) The loan interest rate is calculated at 9% per month and is settled monthly. The loan interest rate for fishery cooperatives may be reduced by 1%. (8) The interest rate for the unloaders of the Fish Market to re-lend to the swimming fresh boats shall not be higher than 3% above the loan interest rate of the Three Banks.

Flour and Wheat Prices Soared Yesterday The Market Added Restrictions on Transactions Temporarily Suspended Forecast: The Rising Trend is Difficult to Stop for a While 145

Central News Agency said that yesterday, the flour and wheat market experienced an even stronger surge. Flour rose by a dime in one day, causing several later sessions to be suspended. Wheat was still flat in the morning, but in the afternoon, due to the sharp rise in flour prices, it also rose by two dimes. The exchange authorities are now trying to find a way to temporarily stabilize the situation, but it is predicted that the rising trend will be difficult to stop in the future. The details of yesterday are recorded as follows:

Soaring Prices Special Restrictions

The rising trend in the flour market has been fierce for days, with a tendency to soar. Yesterday's rise was even greater. After the market opened in the morning, the buying sentiment was very strong, and the demand was huge. Therefore, the prices of all months rose in unison in half a day, reaching as high as seven or eight points. When the market opened in the afternoon, the rising trend did not decrease. The exchange authorities then imposed restrictions based on the "daily price increase shall not exceed one dime" rule. As a result, all months rose by one dime. The highest price for the distant period was three yuan, nine dimes, zero li, two and a half hao, and the highest price for the near period was three yuan, seven dimes, four fen, two li, and a half hao. Since the exchange authorities imposed restrictions on prices, transactions have been virtually suspended.

Wheat Affected Prices Also Rise

Wheat in yesterday's miscellaneous grain market did not fluctuate much when the market opened in the morning. The prices of each month rose by six or seven points. By the most recent sessions in the afternoon, wheat prices also rose sharply due to the high rise in flour prices. Spot and bid prices both rose to six yuan, and distant-period wheat rose to six yuan and six dimes. The near period rose by two dimes compared to the previous periods, and the distant period rose by two dimes, five fen, and six li.

The Market Plans to Seek Stable Solutions

Regarding the sudden rise in flour and wheat prices, the exchange is now looking for stable solutions. For flour, the margin has been increased from 250 yuan to 500 yuan, and it is now planned to increase it to 750 yuan to prevent speculators from manipulating the market. For wheat, the margin will be collected today. If the margin cannot be collected, it may also be suspended from auction.

Insiders Talk About the Reasons for the Sudden Rise

According to inquiries from flour and wheat merchants, the reason for the sudden rise was initially that a certain party bought a large amount of domestic flour. The number of shipments from Shanghai to North China and Northeast China was very large. Although flour mills are working overtime, they cannot meet the demand. Although a certain party has recently stopped buying, there is actually no goods that can be supplied. However, according to this year's domestic wheat production, although it is better than in previous years, in fact, domestic manufacturers have often sought supplies from foreign countries in the past. This year, foreign wheat production is not abundant, and the import of foreign wheat has decreased. Therefore, although manufacturers bought domestic wheat when it was newly produced, the inventory can only supply four or five months. The next new wheat harvest is still nine months away. Therefore, raw materials will be scarce in these four or five months. If we observe the current situation, the future of flour prices is still rising. Moreover, speculators often spread rumors in the market these days, which is also one of the reasons for the rise.

Ministry of Railways Completes Yuehan Railway, Borrows 3 Million from Bank of Communications, Converts 6% British Loan to Formal Debt 152

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Ministry of Railways completed the 6% British Loan for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway in the amount of 1.1 million pounds in the 25th year of the Republic (1936). The loan was underwritten by a syndicate composed of the China-British Banking Corporation and the China Construction Bank. The Ministry of Railways organized a certain Gold Management Committee to issue bonds. On the first of this month, advance subscription certificates were issued first. The official bonds were printed by the Shanghai Commercial Press. The bonds have now been printed, and all who hold advance subscription certificates can exchange them for official bonds at the HSBC at No. 12 Bund starting today. A notice has been issued. As for the insufficient funds for the construction of the Yuehan Railway, it was previously requested that the board of directors in charge of the British Boxer Indemnity Fund transfer the funds earmarked for purchasing materials for the Jinpu and Jiaoji Railways and the funds earmarked for purchasing vehicles for the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway, as well as the second batch of materials for the Capital Ferry. The remaining amount of the British Boxer Indemnity Fund to be returned from the 26th year of the Republic (1937) onwards was used as collateral. Now, as it is still deemed insufficient, another 3 million yuan has been borrowed from the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications. The two banks will bear the burden equally. The funds will be delivered in installments from this month onwards. Both parties have signed a contract, and the funds for this month have already been delivered by the two banks to the Ministry of Railways for distribution to the Yuehan Railway Bureau.

Lu Xun's Remains Were Embalmed Yesterday Afternoon, Funeral and Public Burial at the International Cemetery This Afternoon 154

The remains of literary giant Lu Xun were embalmed yesterday afternoon. The ceremony was simple. The coffin was placed in the ceremonial hall without a lid. Yesterday afternoon and this morning, people from all walks of life continued to pay their respects. The details are as follows:

Still Many Mourners

From dawn yesterday, those who went to the International Funeral Home to mourn and pay respects to the remains continued in an unbroken stream. Some came on foot from far away. There were eighty units from schools and organizations, especially female students, all wearing uniforms of the same color, with orderly ranks and solemn demeanor. Upon entering, they were led into the ceremonial hall by receptionists to pay their respects and circled the remains once before leaving. From 3:00 PM to 4:00 PM, during the embalming process, the mourners all retreated outside. After the ceremony, the mourners paid their respects in turn. The coffin was deep red, made of Phoebe nanmu, and Western-style. It had copper rings all around and an inner lid, half of which was made of glass, revealing the head for people to pay their respects. The coffin was surrounded by wreaths.

Embalming Circumstances

Those present at the embalming included his wife, Ms. Xu, his son, Haiying, his younger brother and his wife, and his daughter, members of the funeral committee Song Qingling, Hu Yuzhi, Kanzo Uchiyama, and friends Zheng Zhenduo, Sachiko Ikeda, and funeral staff, totaling more than thirty people. Yao Shennong served as the master of ceremonies, and a triple bow was performed first, with family members in the front row, followed by members of the funeral committee, staff, and relatives. After the ceremony, his wife, overcome with grief, prostrated herself on the ground and cried loudly, which saddened everyone present. Changing clothes was overseen by the funeral home staff. Mr. Lu Xun wore a white silk shirt and trousers, white socks and black shoes, and a thin cotton coffee-colored jacket and trousers and a long robe. Underneath, he was lined with a cotton quilt of the same color, covered with a scarlet embroidered quilt. After the embalming, his wife and son supported his head, and his younger brother and his daughter supported his feet, and he was placed in the coffin. Finally, family members and others paid their respects in turn. The ceremony was completed at 4:00 PM.

Eulogies and Condolence Messages

Continued recording of elegiac couplets and condolence messages: Wang Xiaolai mourned, "Du Shaoling grieved for hunger and drowning," and "Li Changji vomited out his heart." The Municipal Chamber of Commerce mourned, "A new barrier in the literary world," and "See the immortals on Penglai Island vying to embroider the plains." The Local Association mourned, "A world literary revolutionary, telling his children not to be literary empties, making me ponder endlessly," and "For the popularization of laboring class writing, Mr. made it possible for the canine masses to breathe, why bother about praise or blame." Zhu Jiahao's condolence telegram said, "Upon receiving the news of Mr. Yucai's passing, I am deeply saddened. Mr.'s literary reputation is well-known at home and abroad, and his works are numerous. Who would have thought he would pass away so suddenly? This loss is not only the sorrow of friends. I used to work with him, and our friendship was very close. Thinking of old friends, I feel even more desolate. I hope that his wife and others will restrain their grief. Due to national affairs, I cannot attend the funeral, which I regret." Xu Shoushang wired, "Brother Yucai's death, youth has lost its mentor, the nation has lost its fighter, extremely painful, not only for personal reasons. I hope you will take good care of the orphans and follow his will."

Funeral Route

The funeral will be held this afternoon, and the ceremony has been decided by the funeral committee as follows: (1) The funeral procession will depart from the International Funeral Home at 2:00 PM on the 22nd. (Note: Those from all walks of life who participate in the funeral procession, whether by vehicle or on foot, individually or in groups, please form your own ranks and maintain order. (2) The procession will pass through Jiaozhou Road, Jing'an Temple Road, and Daxilu to Hongqiao Road. (3) At 3:30 PM, arrive at the International Cemetery on Hongqiao Road. (4) At 3:30 PM, people from all walks of life will pay their respects. (5) At 4:00 PM, the burial will take place. The funeral ceremony is simple, and funeral songs will be sung along the way, with free participation by those attending the funeral. The funeral route has been extended at the suggestion of various parties and is planned to detour to Avenue Edward VII, travel east, pass through Route Cardinal Mercier, turn into Avenue Foch, go straight west, pass through Daxilu, and arrive at Hongqiao Road. A temporary decision will be made after contacting the concession authorities this morning.

Funeral Hall Inside the Funeral Home

(Photo by International News Service)

Funeral Arrangements

Continued news: The funeral procession will form at 1:30 PM this afternoon, depart from the International Funeral Home at 2:00 PM, arrive at the International Cemetery at 3:00 PM, and the burial ceremony will be held at 3:30 PM, with interment at 4:00 PM. The funeral procession will consist of: (1) a banner reading "Funeral of Mr. Lu Xun," (2) a wreath team, (3) a elegiac couplet team, (4) a funeral song team, (5) a portrait, (6) a hearse, (7) a family car, and (8) pallbearers: Cai Yuanpei, Song Qingling, Kanzo Uchiyama, etc. As for the funeral ceremony: (1) music, (2) Chairman Cai Yuanpei announces the funeral ceremony, (3) report on his deeds, (4) eulogy, (5) speeches, (6) final salute, (7) funeral songs, (8) burial.

Date of Establishment of People's Organizations Shall Be Based on the Convening of the Establishment Meeting, Term of Office of Staff Shall Be Calculated from the Date of Election, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Ordered to Announce for General Knowledge 159

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs' Proclamation No. 993 states: "According to Municipal Government Instruction No. 20656, which states: 'Approved Interior Ministry Police No. 15, issued on September 30, 25th year of the Republic [1936], No. 00599: Approved Executive Yuan Instruction No. 5587, September 23, 25th year of the Republic: Approved Central Executive Committee Mass Training Division Public Letter No. 4288, September 18, 25th year of the Republic: Approved Hubei Provincial Party Headquarters letter, regarding the Nanzhang County Civil Movement Instructor's request for interpretation of the date of organization and establishment of people's organizations and the first re-election, whether it should be based on the date of election and organization, or the date of oath of office, or the date of approval for record, etc. After reviewing old cases, the explanations are as follows: The organization and establishment of people's organizations should be based on the lawful convening of the establishment meeting, and the term of office of the members should be calculated from the date of election, but if the election of staff of people's organizations requires approval from a higher-level agency according to laws and regulations before it takes effect, then it should be calculated from the date of approval. This matter concerns the organization of people's organizations, and the interpretation of laws and regulations, in addition to sending separate letters, it is appropriate to record the case and forward it for reference, and instruct the competent authorities to take note.' Approved, in addition to ordering the Ministry of Industry to take note, it is appropriate to order your bureau to take note and forward it for information. This order, etc.' Approved, in addition to forwarding to the Public Security Bureau, it is appropriate to order your bureau to take note. This order, etc.' It is appropriate to issue a proclamation for all organizations in this city to be informed. This proclamation."

Shengsi Islands Still Under the Jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province, Results of Meetings of Various Ministries Approved by the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Industry Notified the Ningbo Fellow-Countrymen Association Yesterday 160

Shen Shi News Agency reports that the Ningbo Fellow-Countrymen Association in Shanghai received Notification No. 4470 from the Ministry of Industry's Fisheries Department yesterday, stating: "According to Executive Yuan Instruction No. 6010, October 13, 25th year of the Republic [1936]: Regarding the boundary issue of the Shengsi Islands, it was previously submitted to the ministry and the Ministries of Interior and Finance, as well as the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, for joint review. The report of the review results states that after detailed discussion, the representative of Jiangsu Province advocated that the boundary be set at 32 degrees north latitude (i.e., the Shengsi Islands would still be under the jurisdiction of Jiangsu). The representative of Zhejiang Province advocated that the boundary be set at 30 degrees 53 minutes north latitude (i.e., the Shengsi Islands would be assigned to the jurisdiction of Zhejiang). The representatives of the Ministries of Finance and Industry advocated maintaining the status quo (i.e., the Shengsi Islands would still be under the jurisdiction of Jiangsu). The representative of the Ministry of Interior advocated implementing the two methods decided upon by the ministry in previous meetings (1. All of the Da and Xiao Huanglong Islands would be under the jurisdiction of Zhejiang Province, and Tanhushan and Baishan would be assigned to the jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province. The boundaries of the coastal islands of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces would follow the original boundaries set on the military maps drawn by the Army Survey Bureau. 2. Based on this resolution, the Ministries of Interior and Industry would consult with the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces and then forward it to the Executive Yuan for record). The reasons each held, and a resolution was presented for the President to approve. The current situation should be maintained, and the islands should be under the jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province. In addition to ordering the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to comply and notifying the Ministries of Interior and Finance, it is appropriate to order that you be notified. This notice."

China Agricultural and Industrial Bank Handles Tung Oil Loans, Signs a 200,000 Yuan Agreement with the Zhejiang Construction Department, Yongjia and Other Three Counties Begin Lending 161

After the Zhejiang Construction Department and the Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank in this city agreed on a method for Zhejiang's tung oil production, transportation, and sales loans, the bank began handling it, but only five counties were designated as loan areas. In order to seek universality, the Construction Department contacted the China Agricultural and Industrial Bank and signed a draft agreement for a 200,000 yuan overdraft loan. Farmers in various counties have directly applied for loans from the bank based on the signed draft agreement. Currently, Yongjia, Ruian, and Chun'an counties have begun implementing the loans. The loan amounts range from 10,000 to 30,000 yuan, with an interest rate of 9%, a term of one year, and principal and interest repaid simultaneously upon maturity. All tung oil transportation and sales matters will be entrusted to the Zhejiang Provincial Cooperative Wholesale Society. If the originally planned 200,000 yuan loan is insufficient, negotiations can be held at any time to increase it.

Thoroughly Implement the Anti-Smoking Campaign, Additional Temporary Hospitals Set Up in Each District, Existing Hospitals Find Ways to Increase Beds, So That Smoking Addicts Can Break Their Addiction Early 168

Dagong News Agency reports that since the city's anti-smoking and anti-drug campaign was implemented by order of the Municipal Public Security Bureau on July 20, 24th year of the Republic [1935], for just over a year, the city's anti-smoking campaign has been carried out with propaganda, persuasion, and investigation, and has achieved results. A total of over 50,000 smokers have been registered and licensed, and reported. More than 13,000 people have been sent by the bureau to various municipal drug rehabilitation centers, hospitals, and designated general hospitals for free drug rehabilitation. Since the end of the general inspection of smokers on September 10 in this city, the bureau has issued an order to all branch bureaus to mobilize and conduct house-to-house inspections. Smokers who were missed and not registered have been applying for free rehabilitation in dozens every day. The drug rehabilitation hospitals in each district are full, making it impossible to accommodate the applicants. In order to thoroughly eliminate drugs and enable them to break free from the sea of ​​suffering as soon as possible, the bureau has met with the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee and various hospitals to discuss the results. In addition to the existing and designated hospitals increasing the number of beds for drug rehabilitation offenders, it has been decided that the bureau will consult with various general and specialized hospitals in the city that have not been designated to undertake the implementation of rehabilitation, and will request the Military Commission to allocate funds to set up several temporary hospitals dedicated to providing drug rehabilitation for smoking addicts, so that the city's anti-smoking campaign can be completed as soon as possible.

China International Famine Relief Commission Continues to Provide Agricultural Relief in Shuyang 169

Shuyang in northern Jiangsu has low-lying terrain. Last year, it suffered from severe flooding, and this year, continuous rain has prolonged the submersion of fields, which have not yet been cultivated. Although the accumulated water has receded, due to the aftermath of the disaster, the people are extremely impoverished and unable to purchase seeds, leaving the land desolate. In view of the seriousness of the situation, Dr. Wu Ci, a local Christian pastor, has repeatedly requested the China International Famine Relief Commission at 505 Henan Road in this city to allocate funds for relief. Li Zaiyun, Acting Director of the Agricultural and Irrigation Division, was dispatched to investigate and returned to the commission the day before yesterday to report and submit a relief plan to the Executive Committee for discussion. It is reported that it has been resolved to allocate 10,000 yuan of national currency from the surplus relief funds from the floods of the 24th year of the Republic to purchase and distribute wheat seeds to help with cultivation.

Tuberculosis Screening: Last Month's Statistical Report Shows a Total of 817 People Screened, with Only 246 Completely Healthy 172

The tuberculosis H-ray group screening jointly initiated by the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association and Hongqiao Sanatorium has seen an increase in the number of people screened each month since its inception. According to statistics from last month, from September 11th to October 11th, the total number of people screened was 817, including 626 males and 191 females. In terms of occupation, 339 were from the business community, 233 from the academic community, 36 from the industrial community, 92 from other fields, and 117 were unemployed. The screening results showed that 246 people were completely healthy. Ninety-eight people suffered from active pulmonary tuberculosis, accounting for 13.3% of the total. A total of 413 people were found to have chronic pulmonary tuberculosis, accounting for 50.5% of the total. Sixty people had heart or aortic changes, accounting for 7.3% of the total. According to this, the total number of chronic and active pulmonary tuberculosis cases alone exceeds 60% of the total, which is alarming. Based on Shanghai's population of 3 million, if we extrapolate accordingly, the number of people infected with tuberculosis could reach over 1.5 million. The severity of the disaster is unimaginable. The Xuhui screening center is still located at No. 2 Daxilu, south of Jing'an Temple, with extremely convenient transportation. To facilitate screening for all sectors, it has now been changed to be held every Wednesday morning. Screening certificates can still be purchased from the Shen Bao newspaper office in advance for one yuan per person. Attend at the scheduled time to avoid long waits and crowding.

Drastic Changes in Qingtianjiao Channel Make Navigation Difficult for Yangtze River Vessels; Jiangxin Wheel Captain Telegraphs, Notifying the Customs Measurement Bureau 173

The Yangtze River water level usually recedes in November, but this year, due to the small amount of water in the Sichuan River, the water level in the Yangtze River has also decreased rapidly. Near Jiujiang and above, there are only 21 or 22 feet, and Wuhu only has 17 to 18 feet. In particular, the Qingtianjiao channel in Tongzhou has undergone drastic changes. Yesterday, Huang Youshi, captain of the China Merchants Bureau's Jiangxin Wheel, telegraphed Shanghai, reporting the situation, saying, "This afternoon, this wheel passed the Qingtianjiao buoy. The channel only has 14 feet of ice. The last time this wheel passed this place, it was also during low tide, but there were still 19 feet of water. It can be seen that the channel has undergone rapid changes. Please quickly notify the hydrographic survey, the Customs Port Patrol Department, and all wheels of this bureau to pay special attention when passing through this channel." After receiving this telegram, the bureau, in addition to notifying the captains of all Yangtze River ships, has forwarded it to the Customs and Measurement Bureau to inform all shipping merchants, so as to avoid unexpected dangers for the ships.

Rubber and Cotton Wool Industries Announce Price Increases 174

The rubber, cotton wool, and gauze industries in this city have announced price increases due to rising raw material prices. Details are as follows:

Rubber Industry

The rubber industry issued a notice stating, "According to reports from various member factories, the prices of various raw materials for products have been rising recently, making it impossible to cover costs. Please take swift measures to remedy this in order to maintain capital," and so on. After convening an urgent meeting, a resolution was made that, starting immediately, rubber shoes and ball-running shoes will all increase in price by 5.4.3 jiao per dozen based on the original selling price, according to large, medium, and small sizes, and men, women, and children, in order to maintain capital. Furthermore, with regard to all previous orders accepted by various member factories from customers that have not yet been cleared, it has also been resolved that customers are requested to forgive us and all will be charged at the new price. If we follow the proposal of the previous year, we will request the Social Affairs Bureau to impose penalties. This matter concerns capital, so we hope for your understanding."

Cotton Wool Industry

A joint notice from major factories in the cotton wool and gauze industry, including Datong, Jiansheng, Shanghai, Huisheng, and Zhongmei, states: "Regarding the skyrocketing prices of cotton yarn raw materials, the industry has decided that, starting from October 21st, gauze will increase by 15% of the original price, and cotton wool will increase by 15% of the original price, in order to maintain capital. We hope for your understanding."

Police Department Report: September Crime Statistics 175

According to the Public Concession Police Department's report for September, the number of reported criminal cases in the concession this month was 1,6825, a decrease of 172 cases compared to the previous month and a decrease of 112 cases compared to the previous month. However, compared to the same month last year, there was an increase of 189 cases. The number of criminals arrested this month was 1,308, a slight decrease compared to the previous two months. The number of crimes committed in previous months but arrested this month was 73. The number of arrests made on behalf of other official agencies was 87. In terms of the types of crimes, there were five murder cases this month, one of which was the killing of a Japanese sailor on Haining Road, resulting in one death and two injuries. The murderer escaped from the scene, and three suspects were arrested, two of whom have been released and one is still in custody. There was also a double murder case in a certain obstetrics hospital in Hongkou. In addition, there were two attempted murder cases, three manslaughter cases, and 28 robbery cases, an increase of 15 cases compared to the previous month and an increase of 21 cases compared to the same month last year. There were also 28 burglary cases this month, an increase of five cases compared to the previous month. There were 43 cases of trespassing into homes, an increase of 20 cases compared to the previous month. In addition, according to Group A reports, there were 15 store robbery cases this month, with 15 robbers arrested. There were 93 pickpocketing cases, with 76 pickpockets arrested. A total of 64 bicycles were stolen, with 16 recovered and 16 people arrested. Four cars were stolen, all of which were recovered. In addition, there were 46 snatching cases, with 37 snatchers arrested. Regarding opium suppression, the Central Police Station's opium suppression team handled 20 opium suppression cases this month, detaining 67 opium offenders. Other police stations handled a total of 108 opium cases, detaining 213 opium offenders, of whom 217 were sentenced to imprisonment, five were fined, 54 were released, two had their charges dropped, one Korean was deported to his country, and 21 were in custody. In addition, the Police Department received more than 2,100 reports of violations of traffic regulations, of which 905 were prosecuted in various courts. The rest were given warnings or had their offenses recorded. One hundred and seventeen people were prosecuted for excessive horn honking, including six foreigners and the rest were Chinese. Eight drivers had their licenses revoked for excessive horn honking. A total of 3,316 rickshaw pullers were fined for violations. Eighteen rickshaw pullers who solicited business were revoked of their licenses. Regarding automobile accidents, there were a total of 805 cases this month, including 77 cases of property damage and personal injury, with four fatalities, 504 cases of property damage only, and 224 cases of personal injury only, with two fatalities.

Counterfeit Cigarette Manufacturing Den Broken Up on Faelun Road; Cigarettes Masquerading as Bandits' Brands Sold in the Market 176

Liu Huai, captain of the anti-smuggling team of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, reported on the 16th that Xue Shilin, the squad leader, had received confidential information that someone was setting up an organization in the Zhaojiabang Road area of Nanshi to secretly counterfeit British-American "Bandit" brand cigarettes for sale in the market, hoping to profit from them. He immediately dispatched squad leader Xue and team leaders Liu Bingyuan and Wang Peiting, along with debt investigators, to the Changsheng Hotel opposite the Guandi Temple on Zhaojiabang Road. Guided by the original informant, they arrested Liu Fulin on the spot. He admitted to selling cigarettes outside. Counterfeit cigarette empty cases were found on Liu. After determining the source of these counterfeit cigarette empty cases, the officers went to the Xueji Printing House on Wuhua Road in Zhabei for a raid. They seized a wooden box of cigarette case paper, containing 5,000 sheets, and detained Tang Zongfang, the shop owner. They then went to the third floor of No. 37 Yuanjili, Tangshan Road, Hongkou, and seized four boxes of counterfeit case paper, totaling 20,000 sheets. According to Tang Zongfang, he had partners who specialized in distributing counterfeit cigarettes at Room 15 of the Tongyu Hotel on the 16th Pu in Nanshi. They secretly went to Room 15 of the hotel and arrested Wang Zaide and seized three large boxes of counterfeit cigarettes, totaling 1,500 cigarettes, and many sheets of empty case paper. Wang Zaide confessed that the counterfeit empty cases were entrusted to him by Xu Zhengyuan, who lived at the entrance of Aisi Lane, Qimei Road, Zhabei. The officers rushed to the above-mentioned location and arrested Xu Zhengyuan. Xu pointed out that the empty cases were sold by Jin Zhenyu from Ningbo. As for where the counterfeiting organization was located, he did not know. Until the night before last, the officers secretly went to No. 1 Lianquanfang, Tangshan Road, and arrested Yu Zhenyu. A total of five suspects were arrested, and more than 30,000 sheets of empty case paper were seized. The team interrogated the suspects several times. Jin Zhenyu finally confessed that all the counterfeit cigarettes and empty cases were purchased from a wholesale outlet at No. 769 Faelun Road in the Public Concession. The officers, disguised, went to inquire with Chinese and Western detectives from the police station in charge. They learned that the counterfeiting organization was located at No. 40 Dexin Lane behind Faelun Road. The Chinese and Western detectives entered the house and broke up a huge counterfeiting organization. They captured the resident manager, Gu Yisheng, foreman Li Yuankang, Cao Xianbao, and a certain Japanese, Ikura Ken. Except for Ikura Ken, who was taken away by personnel from the consulate in charge for his own disposal, the other three suspects were transferred to the team. According to their confessions, the person in charge of the organization was actually Jing Huixian and others. All the suspects and evidence have been sent to the bureau for interrogation. The machines seized in the organization have been sealed by the police station for investigation.

Three People Jump into the River, Fortunately All Were Rescued; One Grieved Over National Affairs 177

Between the night before last and yesterday morning, three men jumped into the river to commit suicide. The reasons for their despondency were: one could not bear the pain of illness, one was under economic pressure, and one claimed to be grieving over national affairs. The details of each case are as follows:

Fang Baoyuan, 32 years old, from Ningbo, at 5:10 pm the night before last, took the Chunbei Qianshi ferry at the Peidong Chunjiang Pier to cross the river. When the boat reached the center of the river, he suddenly jumped into the river from the side of the boat. His body was floating up and down. Fortunately, he was rescued by the captain of the boat, who stopped the engine and devised a method of rescue. He was sent to the Customs Water Police Station. He claimed that he was suffering from severe heart pain and that there was no joy in life, so he had the idea of ending his life. The chief police officer immediately sent detective Yao Guofa to Renji Hospital for treatment. Because Fang claimed to have been treated at the Edouard Road Epidemic Hospital, he was sent to the Epidemic Hospital for treatment after being informed by the doctor at Renji Hospital.

Lu Haisheng, 27 years old, from Jingjiang, at 9:10 pm the night before last, stood alone on the Waibaidu Bridge outside the mouth of the Suzhou Creek. Taking advantage of no one's attention, he climbed over the railing and jumped into the river to commit suicide. With a loud splash, waves splashed everywhere. A Chinese police officer from the distant Water Police Station noticed and rushed to rescue Lu. He was taken back to the police station. He confessed that he was a tailor. Because there was no future in his hometown, he admired the prosperity of Shanghai and the ease of making money. Half a month ago, he raised some travel expenses to come to Shanghai and stayed with his friend Chen A'da, who set up a stall on Marong Road in the French Concession. However, after arriving in Shanghai, he could not find a place to eat. His travel expenses were used up, and all hope was lost. He sought death to avoid becoming a starving ghost. The chief police officer, feeling extremely sorry for him, sent detective Xu Lenian to send him to his friend Chen's home to find a way to help him or send him back to his hometown.

Zhuang Binrong, 24 years old, from Hangzhou, jumped into the river at the Zhaofeng Road Pier in Hongkou at 9:00 am yesterday. Fortunately, he was discovered and rescued by a Chinese police officer from the Customs Water Police Station and taken back to the police station. He confessed that he used to work at the Wuhua Silk Weaving Factory and is currently unemployed. He has an older brother named A'bin in Shanghai, who lives in Juxing Lane, Wuhua Road, and runs a teahouse. He was grieved that the country was being oppressed by strong neighbors. He read the newspapers every day and was deeply stimulated. He had a pessimistic view and hoped to die to get rid of his troubles. The chief police officer ordered a detective to summon his brother and take him back to comfort him.

After Bending Down to Pick Up an Apple, a Young Girl Experiences Danger; The Plot is Like a Mythological Novel; The Court Will Conduct a Detailed Investigation 180

Wang Dingtai from Tianjin, who lives at No. 4 Yixing Lane, Guoqing Road, Zhabei, has a daughter named Wang Xiuzhen, 17 years old, who is quite beautiful. On the afternoon of August 16th, she was walking along Guandong Datong Road when she saw two apples on the ground. She bent down to pick them up. An old woman from Suzhou, Wang Hua, stroked the girl's head, and the girl fell into a coma. She was taken to Wang Li's house in Gaoshou Lane, Haining Road, for a night's sleep. She was sweating all over. She woke up in the morning and thanked Ms. Wang for saving her from heatstroke. She asked to be sent home. Ms. Wang hired a car to send her off. Unexpectedly, she became delirious again in the car. She was sent to the Oriental Hotel and raped by a man for two nights. Ms. Wang told the girl that her brother had sold her to him. The girl cried and wanted to see her mother. Ms. Wang took her to the China Hotel at the North Railway Station. Because the girl was crying non-stop, the waiter intervened. Ms. Wang left. A police officer saw her as suspicious and detained her at the Laochan Police Station. The girl explained the situation. The police station thought that the case involved magic, so they arrested Wang Li. Because the incident took place in the Chinese area, they transferred her to the Public Security Bureau and sent her to the Local Court. The prosecutor investigated. In addition to returning the girl to her family, the old woman was also prosecuted. Yesterday, Judge Shao Qinzhi opened the court. The girl confessed the previous situation and said that there were many people watching her in the China Bookstore. The defendant claimed that the girl was her daughter-in-law and that everything she said was completely fabricated. At this point, the victim's lawyer, Tang Hao, appeared in court and filed a civil lawsuit for mental damages of only one yuan. At this point, the official questioned the hotel waiter again. The waiter said that Wang Hua and the girl had been to the Oriental Hotel, but only two people came in and left in the middle of the night, and there was no third person. The official thought that the case needed to be investigated and would be heard again.

Failure to Recommend a Job Leads to Murder; Wu Guangen's Intentions are Sinister; Fang Boxi's Life Ends Tragically 181

Fang Boxi, 24 years old, from Nanhui, was a noodle maker at the Wuweizhai Noodle Shop at No. 9 Minzhuniyin Road in the French Concession. He stayed overnight in the cooking area at No. 12 Xinshou'an Lane, across the street. Because his fellow villager and colleague, Wu Guangen (the same age as Fang), failed to recommend a job to him, Wu harbored resentment and intended to kill Fang. On the night of the 2nd of this month, Wu secretly hid a foot-fighting knife and borrowed a place to stay at Fang's place. At about 5:00 am the next morning, while Fang was sleeping soundly, Wu stabbed Fang's throat with the knife. Fang woke up in pain and chased him out. The police intercepted Wu and took him to the police station. Fang died of excessive blood loss after ineffective treatment. After the body was reported and examined by the court, the police sent Wu to the Special No. 2 Court for interrogation and detention. The Police Department's lawyer prosecuted him for murder under Article 271 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday, Wang Gangxu, the chief of the criminal court of the Special No. 2 Court, and Wang Ren, the prosecutor, came to the second criminal court for a continued trial. Fang Wei, the mother of the deceased, said that her husband had died early and she had raised Boxi. She relied on him for support. Now that he had been killed by Wu, her livelihood was cut off and she requested that the defendant be severely punished. Wu Guangen confessed that he killed him because the deceased did not recommend a job to him, so he was angry and killed him. The court also summoned witnesses Wang Shuyuan and Zhu Fusheng. According to them, the defendant's behavior was usually good, and they did not know why he killed Fang this time. They had never heard him say that he had a feud with Fang. Hua B was summoned from No. 156 and No. 459 to testify about the process of arresting the defendant. At this point, the court considered that the case was clear and ordered the opening of arguments. Yuan Jiahong, the Police Department's lawyer, and the lawyer appointed by the court to defend the defendant made their arguments. The court ordered the debate to be concluded and set the sentence for the 28th. The defendant was returned to custody.
