Fraud for Four Years, Hundreds of Cases, Embezzling Ten Thousand Yuan, All Under the Guise of Hospitals: Police Investigation Completed, Prosecution Initiated 184

Chinese detective Wu Hanzhang of the Putuo Road Police Station No. 50, on the 1st of this month, at the intersection of Huaqing Road and Henan Road, No. 24 Tong'an Lane on Xinzha Road, and No. 59 North Wuxi Road, arrested six individuals: young women Yang Ying, Sun Suzhen, and Sun Cuilan, and men Zhang Xuexiang, Sun Laisheng, and Chen Guantai (also known as Chen Afu or Dou Luan Afu), who were fraudulently soliciting donations from all walks of life under the names of the Guangji Charity Hospital and the Civilian Women and Children Hospital. Along with

Donation Books, Receipts,

etc., they were brought to the First Special District Court for interrogation. Because the defendants were part of a large-scale organized fraud scheme, committing numerous crimes within the concession since 1933, an immediate investigation was impossible. Therefore, it was ordered that they be detained pending further investigation. These details have already been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the police investigation procedures in this case have been completed. The number of cases of fraudulent fundraising committed by the defendants in the concession during these four years is no less than hundreds. The donations obtained,

amount to approximately ten thousand yuan. A secret organization was established, specializing in utilizing young women like Yang Ying, employing their eloquent tongues and disguising them as female students, carrying handbags and donation books, soliciting donations everywhere. The police have now obtained eighteen types of evidence, including: (1) An anonymous letter received by the Gordon Road Police Station on June 6th, enclosing a pamphlet for the Civilian Women and Children Charity Clinic; (2) An

Envelope and Flyer

obtained by Detective No. 50 at Chengshun Porcelain Store, 689 Xihua Road, on September 21st; (3) Thirty-nine envelopes and flyers confiscated when the defendant Yang Xuexiang was arrested, all bearing the words "Guangji Charity Hospital, 1042 Huishan Road, Hongkou"; (4) A ledger from the Guangji Hospital; (5) A receipt book; (6) (7) Two bankbooks; (8) Sixteen cards from the Guangji Hospital; (9) Nineteen business cards of Yang Yunqin (i.e., Yang Ying), an external staff member of Guangji; (10) Two business cards of Hu Weimin, the director of Guangji Hospital; (11) Stamps and receipts

from seventy businesses for donations collected by Yang Ying for Guangji, totaling two sheets; (12) An anonymous letter sent to Judge Fu Lin of the First Special District Court; (13) An anonymous letter sent to the General Inspectorate; (14) A card and receipt from the Civilian Women and Children Clinic, and a receipt from the Guangji Hospital; (15) A receipt from the Women and Children Hospital to Weier Heji Yarn Factory; (16) A card from the Civilian Women and Children Hospital received by the Central Trust Bureau on Hankou Road; (17)

A business card of Xie Weiliang (who can identify the defendant Sun Cuilan) of the General Affairs Department of the Bank of China

on Hankou Road (18) A business card of Xie Kesheng (who can identify Sun Guantai) of the China & South Sea Bank on Hankou Road. These were listed and, along with the defendants, were brought to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang, in accordance with Article 340 of the Criminal Code, charged the defendants with habitual fraud and detailed the case, stating that the first defendant, Yang Ying, admitted to undertaking

fundraising work

since 1933. In 1933, in her hometown of Jiading, she met the defendant Sun Cuilan and came to Shanghai with her, residing with the defendant Chen Guantai. Chen then conceived the idea of ​​fundraising under false pretenses. He accompanied Yang and Sun to Hong Kong, falsely claiming to be from the Shanghai Women's Charity Hospital on Lan Weiai Road in the French Concession, and solicited 2,000 yuan in donations, with Chen paying Yang Ying a monthly transportation fee of 10 yuan. After returning to Shanghai, they again used the names of

the Civilian Women and Children's Hospital

and the Fulu Hospital to solicit donations everywhere, and Yang's monthly salary also increased to 15 yuan. Later, Yang suddenly had a disagreement with Chen Guantai and returned to her hometown last year. In April of this year, she came to Shanghai again, residing at 149 Guling Road. In June, Hu Fengmin, who claimed to be the director of the Guangji Charity Hospital, knowing of Yang's ability to fundraise, invited Yang to cooperate, hiring her as a fundraising specialist, soliciting donations everywhere. Subsequently, because

Yang was falsely using

the names of various hospitals to defraud people of money, someone reported it to the police, and they ordered the Chinese detective of the 50th Precinct to conduct an investigation, which led to the successive arrest of the defendants. Because the defendants were well-informed and knew in advance that the police had begun a secret investigation, they destroyed all the evidence. Now, only one donation book was found at Yang Ying's residence. Since September of this year, she has successively solicited donations from various sectors, reaching more than a hundred households. The police also went to seventy businesses that had been defrauded to investigate, and they all stated that they

had indeed been deceived.

For example, the China Trading Company, the Bank of China, and the China & South Sea Bank on Jiangxi Road could all prove that Yang and Sun had gone to solicit donations. However, because the donations were small, ranging from ten yuan to four jiao, it was considered a charitable act, and the losses were minimal, so they did not come to court. The number of cases committed by the defendants over the years cannot be counted. The police have received anonymous letters indicating that the funds obtained by the defendants amounted to approximately 100,000 yuan. Because the Western detective handling this case must go to the British court to testify in the case of an Indian policeman being shot, it is requested that the trial be postponed, said Detective. Judge Fu ordered Zhang Xuexiang to be released on bail of 300 yuan, and the remaining individuals were returned to detention pending a retrial in seven days.

Xin Chun Chi Bloodshed: Gu Wanfa Dies, Gu Had an Affair with Ni Gengyin's Wife, Ni, Harboring a Grudge, Committed the Murder with an Iron Bar 186

Gu Wanfa, a 50-year-old native of Yangzhou, has been working as a heater and receptionist in the Xin Chun Chi bathhouse at 1379 Lujiabang Road in the Chinese area for many years. Previously, he had collaborated with Ni Gengyin (35 years old this year), a fellow villager and colleague, as a receptionist at Xin Chun Chi. Ni, due to his opium addiction, was lazy in his work and was dismissed by the manager after the January 28th Incident. At the time, Ni mistakenly believed that Gu had secretly instigated his dismissal, harboring resentment. Subsequently, Gu and Ni's wife had an affair, and when Ni was in financial distress, Gu provided some assistance. However, Gu recently encouraged Ni's wife to divorce Ni, which Ni learned of, further fueling his hatred for Gu. On the morning of the 16th of this month, at 5:30 AM, Ni hid an iron bar and, taking advantage of the Xin Chun Chi opening its back door for the cleaner to empty the toilet, seized the opportunity to sneak into Gu Wanfa's area of Xin Chun Chi. Without asking any questions, he pulled out the iron bar and struck Gu's head violently, causing a skull fracture and profuse bleeding. The assailant immediately turned around and fled. The bathhouse staff Kong Qingsong and Xu Zhengshan caught a glimpse of him and tried to pursue the assailant, but it was too late. They immediately informed the accounting office and had Gu taken to Guangci Hospital for treatment. At the same time, they reported to the local Public Security Bureau to dispatch personnel to investigate and apprehend the assailant. However, Gu died from his injuries on the morning of the 18th. Because the incident occurred in the Chinese area and the injured person died in a concession hospital, Xin Chun Chi notified the deceased's nephew, Gu Deshan, who appointed lawyer Zhao Zuwei to file a petition with the Second Special District Court Procuratorate requesting an autopsy. The court ordered the relatives of the deceased to report to the Public Security Bureau to have the body transported to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch. The following day, Prosecutor Wang Ren of the Second Special District Court, accompanied by a forensic doctor and clerk, arrived at the scene at noon to examine the body. Sitting in court, they heard the testimony of the deceased's nephew, Gu Deshan, who stated that he did not know the circumstances of his uncle's assault and death. He was notified by Xin Chun Chi afterward. He now requested to claim the body for burial. Witnesses Kong Qingsong and Xu Zhengshan were not present. The officials declared that Gu Wanfa had indeed died from a head injury caused by the assault. The body was claimed by the deceased's nephew, Gu Deshan, for burial. It was also announced that the case file would be transferred to the Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate for the Public Security Bureau to apprehend the assailant and bring him to justice.

Blood Soul Assassination Squad Members Acquitted by Second Special District Court Because First Special District Court Had Already Sentenced Them, the Crimes Being the Same 187

Liu Hantao, Fu Chaobai, Yin Jiafu, Wang Dongcai, Guan Yaoting, and the other five members of the Blood Soul Assassination Squad, were arrested by the Public Concession Police and prosecuted by the First Special District Court for throwing bombs at shops in the Public Concession to warn them against selling inferior goods. After being sentenced to imprisonment, the French Concession Police transferred Liu and the other five to their custody, believing that they had committed the same crimes in the French Concession. After investigation by the Second Special District Court, it was found that Liu and others had thrown bombs at four locations: Xiedaxiang Foreign Goods Store on Xiaodongmen Street, Yuanhe Sugar Store on Xinkaihe Road, Rixinsheng Foreign Cloth Store on Fa Da Malu, and Bei Runsheng's residence on Beile Road. The Police Department's lawyer then filed a public prosecution based on Article 151, Article 154, and Article 181 of the Criminal Code, alleging crimes such as disturbing public order and endangering public safety. After repeated hearings and deliberations by Judge Chen Shuoying, the debate was declared closed, and a date was set for the pronouncement of the verdict. These details have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday was the date for the pronouncement of the verdict. Around 10:00 AM, Judge Chen arrived at the First Criminal Court and ordered the defendants to be brought before the court. After briefly questioning the defendants about their age and origin, he announced the main text of the judgment: "The defendants in this case are acquitted." He also summarized the reasons for the judgment: "The crimes committed by the defendants are the same as those committed in the Public Concession, and they have already been sentenced by the First Special District Court. Therefore, this court acquits the defendants." After the pronouncement, the defendants were ordered to be temporarily detained in the detention center, pending their transfer back to the First Special District Court for execution of the sentence.

Suspicious Wireless Device on a Xiang Sheng Taxi: The Charterer's Whereabouts Unknown, the Device to Be Sent to the Police Station 188

The Haining Road branch of Xiang Sheng Taxi Company received a phone call around 7:30 AM yesterday morning, stating that they wished to charter a taxi, and the passenger would be waiting at the entrance of Pu'an Lane on Zhoujiazui Road. The branch then dispatched driver Zhang Heshang, a native of Chongming, driving taxi license number 18468. Upon arriving at the entrance of Pu'an Lane, they found a man in his thirties, wearing a gray cloth shirt and pants, waiting for the taxi. After exchanging greetings, the man stated that he had some items to move and asked to wait a moment. After speaking, he turned around and entered the lane. About four or five minutes later, the man came out carrying a newspaper-wrapped object in both hands, placed it on the taxi, and then re-entered the lane. Unexpectedly, he never came out again. The driver waited for a long time, unable to endure it any longer, and was also driven by curiosity. He slightly tore open the paper wrapping to see what was inside, revealing an Eight Lights Feigu brand wireless device, along with a piece of paper that read: "Now sending a wireless device by taxi driver, please check and receive. [Addressed to] Hongkou Police Station." The driver was completely baffled at the time, and he simply drove the taxi to the Hongkou Police Station, reported what had happened, and handed over the wireless device as evidence. After learning the details, the police, fearing there might be other circumstances, immediately dispatched detectives to Pu'an Lane to investigate and investigate the case.

Jiang Hong Returns from Germany to Take Up Position as Engineer in Economic Committee 191

Mr. Jiang Hong, a graduate of the Civil Engineering Department of Tongji University, worked for the Shanghai Municipal Engineering Bureau for three years. In the autumn of 1934, he received a scholarship from the German Humboldt Foundation, so he went to Germany to study water conservancy and road engineering at the University of Munich. In 1935, he obtained an engineering degree and then represented the National Road Association at the International Road Conference, receiving much praise. This year, he served as the president of the Chinese Students Association in Germany, further enhancing his reputation. It is learned that Mr. Jiang has returned to China on the Italian mail ship Aramis, arriving in Shanghai a few days ago. It is also learned that Jiang will stay in Shanghai for a few days and then go to Beijing to take up a position as an engineer in the Economic Committee.

Competing for Foreman Position

After a Violent Beating, He Was Forced into a Poop Bucket, Sun Akang Makes Trouble for Shen Along, and Threatens the Factory Owner by Phone 196

Sun Akang, a native of Jiading, has been working as a foreman at the Tian'an Can Manufacturing Factory at No. 42 Huade Road, earning 34 yuan and 45 jiao per ten thousand cans. The factory was founded by Jiang Zhifu, a native of Ningbo, in 1931 and has been quite successful. Recently, due to a slight decrease in business, the contract price was reduced to 33 yuan per ten thousand cans. Now, Shen Along, a local, contacted the factory owner, Jiang, offering to contract at 31 yuan and 50 jiao per ten thousand. He notified Sun Akang, who refused, so on the afternoon of the 7th of last month, at 3:00 PM, he invited Shen Along to the teahouse at No. 1107 East Broadway Road to discuss the matter, asking him to subsidize expenses on a monthly basis, to continue employing his original eight apprentices, and to pay a monthly contract fee of 45 yuan, before he could take over the contract. Shen, considering the subsidy to be too large, could not resolve it and told the factory owner, Jiang, who dismissed Sun Akang and let Shen Along be the foreman. Around 11:00 AM on the 15th of this month, Sun Akang had someone invite Shen to his house at No. 34 Huade Road under the pretext of talking, and then instigated more than ten people to beat him violently and force him into a poop bucket. After being persuaded to stop, the factory's accountant, Zhu Meisheng, received a phone call asking for the factory owner, Jiang, and claiming that Shen Along had been beaten and that all the costs of installing the machinery when the factory was opened and the unpaid wages, totaling 306 yuan, must be paid in full, or they would use the same means to pay him. Zhu informed Jiang Zhifu, who returned to the factory at 6:00 PM in the afternoon. Jiang Zhifu then reported the matter to the Huishan Police Station, which dispatched detectives to arrest him without success. Sun Akang surrendered to the police in the afternoon with his lawyer. The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Shanghai Municipal Council lawyer Zhang Shizhu explained the case and requested a postponement for further investigation, submitting the two promissory notes to the police station, one for Sun Akang's debt to Shen Along and one for his debt to Jiang Zhifu. Then, factory owner Jiang, accountant Zhu Meisheng, and the assaulted Shen Along testified about what had happened. When questioned, Sun Akang stated that he had been a foreman at the factory since it opened under Jiang's ownership, that the factory initially had only 10,000 to 20,000 yuan in capital but had developed successfully and now had more than 200,000, that he should not be dismissed, and that Shen Along should take over the contract. He also stated that Shen had previously worked for him for six months and denied threatening Jiang by phone. He also stated that Shen's beating was done by others who were dissatisfied and asked for leniency. Judge Xiao Xie Fan ordered him to be remanded in custody, pending further investigation.

Wu Ye Ruizhen Sues Her Brother for Embezzlement, Continued Hearing, Both Parties Instructed to Submit Evidence at the Next Hearing for Review 197

Since Ye Zhongfang, a native of Suzhou, inherited his father Ye Huanyu's position as a comprador in the insurance department of the China Business Company after his death in July, he also took control of all his father's inheritance, which led to his married sister, Wu Ye Ruihua, hiring lawyer Li Zhongwen to file a criminal lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court, accusing him of embezzlement of inheritance, and filed a civil lawsuit to request half of the entire inheritance. The court has summoned him for questioning, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Dai continued the hearing. According to the defendant, Ye Zhongfang, he is the adopted son of Ye Huanyu. The inheritance consists of a house in Suzhou and 1,000 yuan in shares of a certain foreign goods store, all of which are currently managed by his adoptive mother. The deceased father had many concubines during his lifetime, but only one, Madam Xi, has been recognized by the family as his concubine. The plaintiff was raised and married by Madam Xi, and the adoptive mother also has an adopted daughter who has already been married. As for whether the inheritance can cover the debts, he does not know, and he is not currently managing it, so the plaintiff should not be able to receive a share. Madam Xi, Ye Huanyu's concubine, was also present to testify, stating that the plaintiff was brought by Huanyu at the age of twelve and ordered her to raise her. She was only married off this year. Huanyu was quite wealthy in the past, but since he operated the Dafa Chi Bathhouse, he suffered losses year after year, and only left behind a house in Suzhou and 1,000 yuan in shares. The plaintiff, Wu Ye Ruihua, stated that the living expenses of her stepmother in Suzhou were taken from the inheritance when her father died, and that the remaining assets, as Huanyu's biological daughter, she is legally entitled to one-half. The defendant and the married sister, one being an adopted son and the other being an adopted daughter, can only share the other half. However, the defendant's defense lawyer, Hua Maosheng, argued that this kind of inheritance dispute is purely a civil matter, and the plaintiff should not have filed a criminal lawsuit. Since he is accusing of embezzlement, he cannot list the facts of the embezzlement and requested an order for the plaintiff to provide concrete evidence. After reviewing the case, Judge Dai announced a postponement for further hearing on the afternoon of the 30th of this month, instructing both parties to submit evidence for review at the next hearing.

In addition to a thorough investigation by this Bureau, the following is announced for notification: In the future, all households should personally come to the Bureau to pay the fees and obtain a receipt from the cashier's office of this Bureau as proof, to avoid being deceived. Central Bank Inspection Report 201

Central Bank Exchange Coupon Issuance Reserve 305th Inspection Report: This council, in accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, is responsible for inspecting the amount of exchange coupons issued by the bank and the reserve fund. On October 17th of the 15th year of the Republic of China, the 305th inspection was conducted at the bank's head office and branches. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: (A) Total amount of exchange coupons issued: 30,880,061 yuan in silver, including 27,344,3809 yuan in silver yuan coupons and 3,536,2342 yuan in subsidiary coin coupons. Total amount of exchange coupon reserve: 20,880,061 yuan in silver, including 20,313,0651 yuan in cash reserve in silver yuan. The cash reserve is deposited in the bank's head office and branch warehouses and various branches, amounting to 8,597,5670.694 yuan, deposited with peers amounting to 11,337,3944.06 yuan, and the guarantee reserve is equivalent to 10,567,5500 yuan in silver. (B) Total amount of customs gold exchange coupons issued: 400,963.07 yuan. Total amount of customs gold exchange coupon reserve: 400,963.07 yuan. The reserve includes 7,916.290 ounces of pure gold, which is equivalent to 400,963.07 yuan in customs gold at a fixed price of 51.68. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the current reserve shall be at least 60%, and the remainder shall be guaranteed by legal guarantees. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60%, and the guarantee reserve is within 40%, which is in compliance with the law. This is hereby reported. October 19th, 25th year of the Republic of China. Chairman of the Supervisory Committee of the Central Bank: Li Fusun, Supervisors: Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiyin.

Letter 205

To whom it may concern: According to the parties concerned, Gao Yushan and Wu Zhile, after reading the news column in today's "Shen Bao," which contains two news items under the headline "Stealing and Copying Lamp Manufacturing Methods, Hua Yi Sues: Defendants Admit to Copying, Still Awaiting Investigation and Re-examination," the phrase "Defendants have admitted to copying" is not factual. During the court hearing on the morning of October 20th, Yushan absolutely stated that he created it himself and succeeded as early as the year before last, so there was no need to copy other people's methods. Zhile also only stated that he saw the announcement in the Industrial Bulletin and copied it publicly, which is completely different from admitting to copying. This can be verified by court records. However, "Shen Bao" has recorded it in this way, which is obviously inconsistent with the facts. We should request a written correction to clarify the true facts. This is a matter of public justice. To the chief editor of "Shen Bao," Lawyer Yu Hualong, October 21st, 25th year.

Era Medicine Publication

Marital Knowledge

— Written by Dr. Yao Erchang, Medical Doctor of Ben Xue Weni University, America

Health is the Pillar of Marital Bliss 208

...When men and women begin to develop, they need knowledge to guide them into the paradise of life ... Sexual dysfunction is an evil that robs couples of happiness and is unique to weak youth ... Tobacco Shop 215

— Rong

Stepping out of the alley entrance, it seems brighter; those dozen or so shops that have been closed for half a year, suddenly the one near the alley entrance is surrounded by many people. The newly painted counter is still emitting a pungent smell, and a sign is hanging in front of the door, densely written with rows of small characters. The top row is the brand of cigarettes, and below are soap, thread, and all kinds of daily necessities. There are three or four shop assistants busy greeting customers. I am quite happy for the owner of that tobacco shop for this rare liveliness. Because every day I step out of the alley entrance, I always wonder

Page 20

why no one comes to open such a shop. More than a hundred households living in this alley would feel it is too troublesome to go to the opposite street to exchange money, and many daily necessities for households in Shanghai's alleys depend on the tobacco shop. No matter how bad the market is, this sign is still a good business.

Going home in the evening, they haven't closed yet. I am used to seeing a row of dark shutters every day, and this sole shop standing there looks quite outstanding. At this time, a bald middle-aged man is serving customers in the shop. Seeing that I am a customer jumping off a rickshaw, he greets me with a smiling face:

"Sir, do you live in the alley?"

I nodded and casually asked, "Is business good?"

"Thank goodness! Thank goodness!" He drums on his bald head, which is the unique attitude of Chinese merchants, while counting the coppers for my exchange.

In this way, in less than three days, we have become very familiar. Whether exchanging coppers or buying cigarettes, we have to exchange a few words, and he is especially polite to me. For example, when exchanging coppers, although the sign clearly says it exchanges at 9.9 cents per yuan, he gives me the full amount. The old hands who run tobacco shops calculate carefully on coppers. One yuan, from cents to coppers, is at least four or five coins different from directly exchanging coppers. The first time he exchanged ten dimes for my yuan, I felt very sorry and added three more coppers, but he refused to take them no matter what:

"Living in the same alley, taking care of the small shop's business makes up for it!"

After a few more days, the two boxes of cigarettes that I am used to buying for twenty cents each, he gave me two coppers back. I hesitated and looked at his smiling bald head, and then looked at the sign above, which specially marked the prices of various cigarettes in red powder, each one being one coin less than usual.

"Price reduction?" I asked him.

"Big price reduction! Big price reduction!"

But the tone of his voice and the smiling face are not consistent. Seeing that his eyes are always looking at the opposite street, I turned my head to look, and it turned out that the sign of the tobacco shop on the opposite street was marked with very large characters in red powder. Although I can't see the prices on it clearly, I already understand that the two competitors are fighting there.

The next day, when I stepped out of the alley entrance, I was attracted by a large sign in front of the counter of the tobacco shop on the opposite street. Each bar of Guben soap was marked with fourteen coins, the nine characters being as big as bowls. This is naturally another sign of a big sale, but I have never known the real price of this kind of thing, so it is naturally inexplicable how much cheaper fourteen coins per bar is than usual. Looking at the front of the bald head's counter, there is also a similar large sign, which says twenty-two bars of Guben soap per yuan. I calculated in my stomach that at the exchange rate of 3,010 cash, it would be another seven coppers cheaper.

"Old Guan," I asked him when buying cigarettes, "The loss these past two days is not small, right?"

He wiped his hand from his bald head and spat:

"Really want to save face and live like a ghost! Selling Guben soap for fifteen coppers still doesn't have much profit – that's just to respond to the market. Selling ass, selling it for fourteen each! Fine! Twenty-two yuan for one yuan, calculate it, 3,080."

He shook his head, indicating that our boss has a lot of capital and doesn't care about losing a few coins.

I walked away smiling.

They sing duets every day, and many items, even I, an amateur, know are cheaper than the purchase price. Sometimes, the sign for exchanging foreign currency suddenly increases by several coppers compared to the market price, and everyone in the alley is discussing where the two bosses offended each other.

One morning, stepping out of the alley entrance, the bald head's tobacco shop had dark shutters up again. The large sign on the opposite street has naturally been taken in, and the prices on the sign in front of the door have probably returned to their original prices, right?

In the first few days, I often stopped the car at the alley entrance and reluctantly went to the opposite street to exchange coppers. The trouble is secondary. Seeing every face in their shop, I immediately think of that bald head shaking his head, "Want to save face and live like a ghost!" It seems that the angry look of him wiping his hand from the bald spot and spitting is rippling in front of my eyes.

Autumn Harvest, Winter Storage 216

— Written by Ma Mengchen

Small Street 217

— Shen Jiaqian

Yesterday, the night train arrived at × county, and I got to the inn at 2:00 AM. After sitting on the train for a whole day, my back and waist were sore. Seeing the bed, I immediately wanted to lie down and relax my limbs that had suffered a day's imprisonment. But when I asked the porter here, the first gasoline boat would leave at 5:00 AM, and the inn was half an hour away from the dock. Counting on my fingers, there would be at most two hours to sleep after deducting the beginning and the end. Everyone discussed and prepared to sacrifice to the end, and sleep on the boat. It would be very easy to sit for two hours. We told the porter our idea and asked him to find some wine and dishes for us. Originally, we should have put some food into our stomachs at this time. Our dinner was a plate of egg fried rice that looked like a decoration before getting on the train.

But that thin porter had quite a bit of experience in catering to guests from other provinces. He said that small places have small situations, and there are really no shops to buy things in the middle of the night, and the inn doesn't sell wine or food. He said that if the gentlemen were happy, he could take us to a place. As he said this, he deliberately shrunk his head and stuck out his tongue, that kind of sneaky appearance would make people think of the clown with a white nose on the stage.

Of course, there was no need for him to explain in detail what a good place that was. Everyone already understood it. So the three of us held another meeting. To investigate in this small market town (these two words might be too official, but we really had this intention.) The situation of those poor insects who were being squeezed by life might not be a completely boring act. We immediately agreed to the porter. At the same time, we didn't plan to return to the inn anymore, so we entrusted him with the luggage and asked him to deliver it to the dock before five o'clock, and there would be a generous reward.

That porter was extremely happy, and answered with a series of "Yes! Yes! Yes!" in a heavy nasal voice. He also specially returned to the small room to put on a long gown, lit a horse lamp, secretly communicated with a small waiter sleeping on the counter, and led us onto the street.

The street was as if it were dead, and there wasn't even the sound of dogs barking. The distance between a few kerosene street lamps was always more than four or five zhang. We paid attention to the circle of light illuminated by the horse lamp, and walking was almost like surveying the terrain.

Just as we were about to turn into a small alley, we met a policeman on duty. The porter chatted with him for a while using a kind of "code" that we didn't understand, and let us pass.

I'm not deliberately exaggerating about that small alley. If someone is a little wider, their shoulders will suffer a bit of damage. The porter told us that it's called Small Street, and it's the small base of prostitutes. The fact that the prostitutes here have to donate a few dollars of flower donation every month should be a public agreement, but if the policeman on duty finds out that someone is keeping a guest overnight, they will ask you to sit inside for a night. Although you will have to spend a little "exit fee" the next day, the "business" is getting worse and worse. The policeman we met deliberately "patrolled" at the corner of Small Street, which is what that means.

After walking past ten or so broken houses, the porter stopped in front of a house with a number 12 kerosene lamp. The door was ajar, and we followed him in. After passing through a foul-smelling patio, perhaps they had already heard our footsteps inside, and a young girl came out to greet us. She first talked to the porter before asking us to sit inside. The porter asked us for two dollars, explaining that he had to split it with the policeman on duty.

That room can be described with the four words "messy and disorganized." Apart from this "extra money" of ours, I thought that if the guests who come here don't come specifically to stay overnight, then there must be too few places to spend money in this market town. That little girl probably saw that we were guests from other provinces, and was busy making tea and putting out two plates of melon seeds and peanuts, and loudly called her mother to go outside to watch, and if the policeman on duty came, He Er (the porter's name) had already given a greeting.

When He Er was about to leave, he specially whispered in my ear: "If anything happens, He Er will guarantee it. Let the gentlemen enjoy themselves." Then he shrank his head, stuck out his tongue, and left carrying the horse lamp. (To be continued)

The impression you gave me is too deep. I can't forget you. The knowledge you gave me is too true. I can't forget you. I now swear that I would rather die. Never to be separated again. Having tasted enough of separation. I can't forget you. Thinking of your smiling gaze. I can't forget you. Thinking of your considerate tenderness. I can't forget you. Your image is deeply rooted in my heart. Difficult to eliminate for a long time. Even if I am buried in the soil. I can't forget you. Thinking of your shy silence. I can't forget you. Thinking of your deep affection and sweetness. I can't forget you. I won't forget every smile you have. The impression you gave me is too deep. I can't forget you.

Storytelling 222

Cao Xiaoying's Jade Dragonfly

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Romance of the West Chamber"

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

A scholar's friendship is worth half a sheet of paper. An ounce of silver prepares a meditation hall. The most precious are the three treasures of the land. Meditating in Zen, listening to the explanation of the Diamond Sutra. The lonely cuckoo cries beside my ears. The alien inn is even more desolate. This place is, Clear wind and bright moon are unattended. Rest your shoulders and stay in the West Chamber. Sitting idly in the small pavilion to understand the principles of Yi. Opening a book by the firefly window, reciting articles. A pair of vulgar and noisy words. Walking out of the green-clad maid. To comply with the command of Madam Cui. Specially set up a dojo in the Zen room. First, the late Lord's death anniversary. Please recommend the monk to the West. Fifteen good days to worship the Dharma King. After speaking, wanting to leave, stopping. To pass on the love-struck fan to the powdery man. Zhang Sheng leaned over and bowed deeply. Elder sister is, Could it be Red Maid, Miss Yingying's maid. I am, Zhang Junrui, a talented scholar from Luoyang. Made a study in the monastery for marriage. Please report from the Rui Zhu Palace. Saying, There is no wife in the family yet. Red Maid hears. Changing her face. Your words are too absurd, sir. It has been said from ancient times that one should not speak of impropriety. Reading gentlemen love frivolity. The old lady has a frosty temperament. Children three feet away are not allowed to enter the hall. Speaking of maids can be forgiven. The Madam knows and hates very much. You must think carefully before you speak from now on.

Chen Lianqing and Qi Lianfang's Little Money

New Sound (1380) 6:00 PM to 7:00 PM

Opening Chapter "Xiangyun Sleeps on Stone"

The fourth month of the Grand View is drunk in the flower season. Peonies are blooming everywhere. The order belongs to Qinghe, and the flowers are still good. Brother Bao's birthday is set up with a flower feast. The Hongxiang flower garden is brightly opened. People come under the flowers, full of joy. Drumming to urge the flowers, ordering wine. Borrowing flowers to offer Buddha, writing poems together. A beauty, after the feast, foggily looks for the flower path. Fluttering steps like a flower fairy. Flowers know people's intentions and add charm frequently. Intoxicated by the flowers, leaning on the stone to sleep. The flowers seem to be affectionate and pity the drunken state. Remnants of flowers protect the body, soft as cotton. Not knowing the fallen hairpin at the bottom of the flowers. People come to the flower path to pick up the emerald hairpin. The flower face is good. The drunken state is upside down. People are drunk and flowers are blooming, both beautiful. Flowers must be less colorful because of drunk people. People become more beautiful because of flowers. Don't suspect the bees and butterflies playing with flowers. A waist is caressed, and the flowers also pity. Birds sing in the flowers, breaking the dream. The sisters of all the flowers arrive in front of the flowers. Peach face is ashamed and hard to hide. Just tidying up the appearance of the flower, holding hands and spinning. The flowers and the moon in the Red Chamber will always flutter.

Movie

Nanjing Grand Theatre Friday Public Screening "Spring in the Maiden's Heart" 223

"Spring in the Maiden's Heart" is the most elaborate production of Universal Company this year. When it was screened in the United States, all newspapers unanimously believed that the film was the most humorous masterpiece of abundant jokes since the invention of sound films. The story in the film is based on the novel by the famous novelist Irick Heisch. It narrates the various scandals and strange appearances in the homes of the rich. There are all kinds of things, and there is nothing that is not strange. The humor of the dialogue and the slapstick of the action can really make people laugh and cry when they see it. The protagonist of the film is William Powell, who has always been good at playing gentleman-type roles. In this film, William appears on the screen in another guise. The first half plays a desolate scavenger in the slums, and the second half plays the steward of a wealthy family. The supporting actors include Carol Lombard and Elias Brody.

Xinhua Scenery Line 224

China's first horror blockbuster, "Midnight Song," has attracted much attention from movie fans. The film has unique features in photography and sound.

Jinshan's makeup in "Midnight Song": with a hideous face and withered fingers, it is almost the resurrection of a corpse. When silent, it makes people shudder.

After "Happy Night," Shi Dongshan will make greater efforts to direct "Bells of Huangshan," written by Tian Han. The selection of the protagonist and the location of the exterior scenes have been prepared and will be filmed soon.

There is a song in "Little Orphan Girl," sung by Chen Juanjuan, with a sad tone that evokes sympathy.

For the sake of amateur learning, Xinhua colleagues have set up a library and welcome donations of books and newspapers from various magazine clubs. They are willing to exchange with Xinhua Pictorial to express their gratitude.

Xinhua Pictorial is gradually becoming perfect. The content of pictures and texts in the fifth issue is more substantial, and the cover and binding are unique and stylish. The first edition of 12,000 copies has been sold out soon.
